  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer8724677818476718645"><b>"Agatha Christie meets Groundhog Day . . . quite unlike anything I’ve ever read, and altogether triumphant.” - A. J. Finn, #1 New York Times-bestselling author of The Woman in the Window</b><br/><br/>Aiden Bishop knows the rules.   <span id="freeText8724677818476718645" style="display:none"><b>"Agatha Christie meets Groundhog Day . . . quite unlike anything I’ve ever read, and altogether triumphant.” - A. J. Finn, #1 New York Times-bestselling author of The Woman in the Window</b><br /><br />Aiden Bishop knows the rules. Evelyn Hardcastle will die every day until he can identify her killer and break the cycle. But every time the day begins again, Aiden wakes up in the body of a different guest at Blackheath Manor. And some of his hosts are more helpful than others. With a locked room mystery that Agatha Christie would envy, Stuart Turton unfurls a breakneck novel of intrigue and suspense.<br /><br />For fans of Claire North, and Kate Atkinson, <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is a breathlessly addictive mystery that follows one man's race against time to find a killer, with an astonishing time-turning twist that means nothing and no one are quite what they seem.<br /><br /><b>This inventive debut twists together a thriller of such unexpected creativity it will leave readers guessing until the very last page.<br /><br />Recommended in <i>The New York Times</i>, <i>The Guardian</i>, <i>Harper's Bazaar</i>, Buzzfeed, Vulture, BookRiot, and more.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8724677818476718645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi there, sorry - I didn't realise this page existed! Yes, 'Seven Deaths' and '7 1/2 Deaths' are exactly the same. We had a clash in the US and had to<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi there, sorry - I didn't realise this page existed! Yes, 'Seven Deaths' and '7 1/2 Deaths' are exactly the same. We had a clash in the US and had to change the title there, hence 7 1/2. Don't worry, you're getting exactly the same amount of murder for your money, though. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2468654200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2468654200" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2468654200?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408889565" href="/book/show/35967101-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-thriller-mystery">adult-thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2468654200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14898853327941668021">I didn't expect to tear through this book, but I did—there was just so much restlessness in my reading, an <em>urgency</em> to reach the ending. It’s been days and I am still so keenly, strangely, extensively aware of explosions still taking place inside my head. Honestly? If Hollywood doesn't turn this into a movie....I will personally riot.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>So, what's this book about?</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Our narrator wakes up in a dripping forest, with nothing but the shade of an old unnameable fear, and the eerie sensation of b</span>
  <span id="freeText14898853327941668021" style="display:none">I didn't expect to tear through this book, but I did—there was just so much restlessness in my reading, an <em>urgency</em> to reach the ending. It’s been days and I am still so keenly, strangely, extensively aware of explosions still taking place inside my head. Honestly? If Hollywood doesn't turn this into a movie....I will personally riot.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <u>So, what's this book about?</u>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />Our narrator wakes up in a dripping forest, with nothing but the shade of an old unnameable fear, and the eerie sensation of being followed, an invisible gaze locked on his back. He has no recollection of who he is, and he has no more notion how he got there than he did the moon. But his head is firing thought after thought that can’t seem to complete themselves and they all begin with a name: <em>Anna</em>, and never seem to end.<br /><br />He later learns that his name is Aiden Bishop and he’s trapped inside a stranger’s body. A masked figure curtly informs him that he must unveil a murder disguised as to not look like one if he wants to earn his release, and <strong>he must do so by reliving the day of the murder eight times, but each morning he will wake up in the body of a foreign soul.</strong> If he fails to uncover the name of the would-be murderer, he will return to the first day, memory moped clean, and start all over again as he has apparently already done innumerable times before.<br /><br />Matters are made worse when Aiden realizes he isn’t the only one carried so long here and there on a stream and washed now to this strange shore: two other people are also ensnarled inside this time loop, and a knife-wielding Footman is out for their blood.<br /><br />Aiden, Anna and the anonymous rivals are pieces on the game board, and there is <em>everything</em> at stake.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>Normalcy has its place, but you won't find it in this book.</strong><br /><br /><em>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</em> is a dazzling, mind-bending murder mystery…<em>without a murder</em>. It’s a locked-room thriller with a nearly imperceptible warp wavering in its center. A brilliantly balanced knife's edge of a book—unfolding gradually but deliberately, with secrets unveiled as more lies are told. Every sentence was a labyrinth to navigate and my mind often felt like a door blown open in a storm. The whole experience of reading this book felt like an elaborate lie to me, some made-up fantasyland I was locked in for a set number of hours a day. And like Aiden, every moment, I was caught between another dead end and another lead.<strong> So many pieces of the story but how the hell do they fit together?</strong><br /><br />In richness of ideas, and in glory of sentences, this book is spectacular. I was deeply impressed by the sense of scope, the minute turnings of characters and their choices and how those ripples affect other players, by the hints strewn like breadcrumbs throughout the narrative and the puzzle pieces that were constantly moving around. This was genuinely brilliant and so intricately crafted and I’m still left marveling at how one person’s brain can contain multitudes.<br /><br /><em>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle </em>might be focused on the story of Aiden Bishop but the stories of many others are caught up in the wheel of his, and as that wheel turns, so do these many intertwined lives and fates. The narration lingers in the memories and lives of each “host”, dipping in and out of them like toes in a pool. The book makes you question what you know about these characters, their lives and their secrets. <strong>Everyone is unreliable, everything is questionable.</strong> Aiden’s very sense of self is threatened to be overruled by the personalities of his hosts, most of which were nasty pieces of work: more than slightly sexist, selfish, mean, manipulative, abusive, more often than not physical and moral cowards—yet still compelling even when you can’t bring yourself to like them even a little bit, and I think that says a lot for the author’s skill.<br /><br /><em>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</em> corkscrews into a tighter and tighter coil with every page and it isn't long before Aiden’s constant picking at the stray threads of his new jarring reality makes the whole come apart, revealing far more than was ever dreamt of. <strong>I did not see that ending coming at all,</strong> and I was left astounded into an awed slow-clap at everything the author has accomplished here.<br /><br />When I flipped that last page, all I could do was breathe out, with the kind of eloquence and poise perfectly befitting the situation: "Holy shit. What did I just read?"<br /><br /><blockquote>❗️<strong>TRIGGER WARNINGS</strong>❗️ fatphobia, murder, suicide, discussions around rape and sexual abuse, alcohol and drug use.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14898853327941668021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2665337125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2665337125" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2665337125?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2665337125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16816291569374795802"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587946960i/29363149._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u> <a href='https://youtu.be/efJYd7l7LGE' rel='nofollow noopener'>CLICK HERE for a Booktube Video</a></u></b> about:<br/><br/>Ten Fabulous Book Reviews and One That Will Make You Go - <i>doesn't that belong to Miranda Reads?</i><br/><br/>Now that you know this one made the list check the video review to see the rest (and find the stolen surprise)!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b> <br/><br/><i>Read this one for TCE book club! </i><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566618567i/28042651._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>If this isn’t hell, the devil is surely taking notes.</i>
</blockquote>Lord and Lady Hardcastle are throwing a "party" at Blackheath, their crumbling British mansion.<br/><br/>This so-called-party takes place on<b> the anniver</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16816291569374795802" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587946960i/29363149._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u> <a href="https://youtu.be/efJYd7l7LGE" rel="nofollow noopener">CLICK HERE for a Booktube Video</a></u></b> about:<br><br>Ten Fabulous Book Reviews and One That Will Make You Go - <i>doesn't that belong to Miranda Reads?</i><br><br>Now that you know this one made the list check the video review to see the rest (and find the stolen surprise)!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b> <br><br><i>Read this one for TCE book club! </i><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566618567i/28042651._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>If this isn’t hell, the devil is surely taking notes.</i>
</blockquote>Lord and Lady Hardcastle are throwing a "party" at Blackheath, their crumbling British mansion.<br><br>This so-called-party takes place on<b> the anniversary of their son's murder</b> (19 years ago), includes the exact same guests as it did so many years ago.<br><br>And, during the night, trusts will be violated, truths will be exposed and above all, their daughter, <b>Evelyn Hardcastle will be murdered.</b><br><br>Aidan Bishop, along with two others, <b> are in competition</b> to be the first to discover Evelyn Hardcastle's murderer.<blockquote>
  <i>Too little information and you're blind, too much and you're blinded.</i>
</blockquote><b>Bishop relives the night of Evelyn's murder</b> for eight days, and each day he is in a different body and has a new chance to find the murderer. <blockquote>
  <i>Life doesn’t always leave you a choice in how you live it.</i>
</blockquote><b>The first day, </b>Bishop wakes up in Dr. Sebastian Bell's body, without a clue as to where he is and what he is supposed to do.<br><br><b>The second day, </b>Bishop wakes up in the butler's body...but "past-Bishop" is also inhabiting Bell's body. Which leads to a lot of confusion and surprise.<br><br><b>The third day, </b>there's current-Bishop, past-Bishop and past-past-Bishop....well you get the point. <br><br>Each day Bishop adds another "character" under his belt. He gets<b> eight bodies, and eight days,</b> to piece together the mystery. <br><br>The two others who are in competition with Bishop are unknown to him and are also inhabiting bodies (though, unlike him, they cannot swap and every "day" their memories reset). <br><br>They are all racing to find out the murderer, because whoever can figure out this mystery is the winner.<br><br>And the winner? <b>
  <i>The winner gets to escape.</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?</i>
</blockquote>This book was confusing in the best way possible.<br><br>I could barely write my summary - there's just so many layers of <b>complexity and betrayals and everything.</b><br><br><b>So <i>effing </i>impressed. </b><br><br>I was wholly ensnared by the mystery - I hardly knew what to think or where to look - but it was such a <b>fun and wild ride</b> that I didn't care.<br><br>Aiden Bishop was a <b>wonderfully fleshed-out character</b> and Turton did a particularly excellent job with the various bodies that Bishop possessed.<br><br>In particular, I loved how each body Bishop possessed would begin to influence him. When he was Dr. Sebastian Bell, Bishop was meek, under the butler's influence Bishop became moralistic and so on. <br><br>It was fascinating to watch how that played out.<br><br>The only thing that <b>threw me slightly </b>was the end. The build to the climax and the ending were superb...but the actual grand reveal was a bit of a letdown.<br><br>I honestly don't know what I as expecting, just something a bit "more" - if that makes any sense...<br><br>All I know is that this is an author to watch. <b>
  <i>I cannot wait to see what Turton writes next!!</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>We are never more ourselves than when we think people aren’t watching.</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Rather well-read, a thoroughly enjoyable book to listen to!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2332976608?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40033006-the-7-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332976608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3701864804054334730"><i>Too little information and you're blind, too much and you're blinded.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590682850ra/29556402.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The above-quoted line, perfectly sums up the <s>MIND F**KERY</s> literary puzzle that is <i>The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>.<br/> <br/>Let me be clear, this book is <b>bloody FANTASTIC</b>!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471110715ra/20002905.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Never have I been so excited by being so confused whilst reading a book!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468893184ra/19756087.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Turton is a Master. <br/><br/>This was completely original, completely out there and completely compelling. I was so absorbed in every moment and....well, <b>CONFUSED</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542821993ra/26630247.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There is really not much I can say ab</span>
  <span id="freeText3701864804054334730" style="display:none"><i>Too little information and you're blind, too much and you're blinded.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590682850ra/29556402.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The above-quoted line, perfectly sums up the <s>MIND F**KERY</s> literary puzzle that is <i>The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>.<br> <br>Let me be clear, this book is <b>bloody FANTASTIC</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471110715ra/20002905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Never have I been so excited by being so confused whilst reading a book!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468893184ra/19756087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Turton is a Master. <br><br>This was completely original, completely out there and completely compelling. I was so absorbed in every moment and....well, <b>CONFUSED</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542821993ra/26630247.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is really not much I can say about the plot of this novel without getting all spoilery. I recommend going into this knowing as little as possible.<br><br>This being said, you should be aware of the fact that it is okay to be reading it and not understanding anything that is going on. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449599269ra/17310841.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The longer it goes, the more info you have and the more confusing it can become. It's <b>exceptional</b> in its detail. <br><br>I had so many theories, some panned out, others didn't but I never stopped guessing, right up until the very end.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1535257835ra/26200820.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you are looking for a completely unique mystery to get you through the holiday season, look no further. <br><br>Stop right here! <br>This is the book you need to read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551861937ra/27161369.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot wait to read more from Stuart Turton. I am already fangirling over him after one book. <br>I just love his ingenuity and style. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571050269ra/28291185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you so much to the publisher, Sourcebooks Landmark, for providing me a copy to read and review. <br><br>I am blown away!!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5956266012439860714">(4.5) If you’re looking for a book to keep you awake at night because you NEED to finish it then this is it!<br/><br/><i>Somebody’s going to be murdered at the ball tonight. It won’t appear to be a murder so the murderer won’t be caught. Rectify that injustice and I’ll show you the way out.</i><br/><br/>I loved how unique the premise was, a murder-mystery where the main character gets to relive the same day 8 times to try and solve it but every day he's in a different body. <br/>It was also interesting to see how the different</span>
  <span id="freeText5956266012439860714" style="display:none">(4.5) If you’re looking for a book to keep you awake at night because you NEED to finish it then this is it!<br /><br /><i>Somebody’s going to be murdered at the ball tonight. It won’t appear to be a murder so the murderer won’t be caught. Rectify that injustice and I’ll show you the way out.</i><br /><br />I loved how unique the premise was, a murder-mystery where the main character gets to relive the same day 8 times to try and solve it but every day he's in a different body. <br />It was also interesting to see how the different bodies/personalities affected the story and there were twists I didn’t see coming. <br /><br />I was feeling a reading slump creeping in and this book fixed it so I’m rounding it up to 5 stars.<br /><br />Would recommend if you’re in the mood for a mystery with a sci-fi twist to it!</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184345183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5370825845369019938"><b><br/>3.5 maybe it is just me? But never the less confusing stars🌟🌟🌟</b><br/><br/>The concept of this book was really quite brilliant... A little reminiscent of both <i>Life After Life</i> and <i>Ground Hog Day....</i> with the added little twist of the body swapping....<br/><br/>Admittedly it is holiday time and I was not as focused on this book as I needed to be.... so as far as me being confused throughout the majority of this book, it could very likely just be a me problem.... I kept needing to go back and reread parts because I reall</span>
  <span id="freeText5370825845369019938" style="display:none"><b><br />3.5 maybe it is just me? But never the less confusing stars🌟🌟🌟</b><br /><br />The concept of this book was really quite brilliant... A little reminiscent of both <i>Life After Life</i> and <i>Ground Hog Day....</i> with the added little twist of the body swapping....<br /><br />Admittedly it is holiday time and I was not as focused on this book as I needed to be.... so as far as me being confused throughout the majority of this book, it could very likely just be a me problem.... I kept needing to go back and reread parts because I really got lost as to what body Aidan was in at what time..... I was also a little bit overwhelmed keeping track of all the characters and what part they played in the story, but again it could have been me!<br /><br />I liked the premise, I really was intrigued by the mystery, I just was not invested enough to probably grasp the full concept.... additionally I had a huge expectation of a fabulous ending that would make all of this make complete sense to me, and that sadly did not happen for me.....<br /><br />So while I found this book very clever in concept, I found it a little... ok really a lot confusing for me.... The good news is this book is not released until September, so I might give it another chance this summer when I can be a little more focused and give it the proper attention it probably deserves...<br /><br />*** i’d like to thank Net Galley and the publisher for a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review ***<br /><br /> This was a buddy read, that left Norma, Marie Alyce, and myself baffled... truly think it was bad timing, definitely not a holiday read! But thanks ladies for making me realize I was not alone in this! 😘<br /> </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13150874804562275789"><b>Reading <u><i>The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i></u> left me MIND BLOWN!</b>🤯 What an intricately layered and amazing plot. If you haven't read this one yet, please jump into this book blindly and savor every moment. At times you will feel like you are flailing in the water, drowning in confusion. Just keep reading, treading through the chapters as you go. Grab hold of the bits that are sent your way and store them. It will all make sense in the end!<br/><br/>I thought I was prepared for Turton. I read carefully, gi</span>
  <span id="freeText13150874804562275789" style="display:none"><b>Reading <u><i>The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i></u> left me MIND BLOWN!</b>🤯 What an intricately layered and amazing plot. If you haven't read this one yet, please jump into this book blindly and savor every moment. At times you will feel like you are flailing in the water, drowning in confusion. Just keep reading, treading through the chapters as you go. Grab hold of the bits that are sent your way and store them. It will all make sense in the end!<br /><br />I thought I was prepared for Turton. I read carefully, giving the book my full attention. I even re-read parts to be sure I understood what I thought I was meant to understand. Still, I did not fully see where I was being led. <b>This was an outstanding literary puzzle!</b> It was not only an expertly crafted whodunnit, it truly ends up being so much more. 5 ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ and I'd give it more if I could. I love to be challenged and surprised by a book and this one did that and then some. 🙌🏽<br /><br />What a debut! I can not wait to see where Turton's mind takes us next. I'm there for it!<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Stuart Turton, Sourcebooks Landmark and NetGalley for an advance copy to read in exchange for my honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_2296946869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296946869" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296946869?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296946869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7723345074377891101"><i>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is a thriller following an investigation into the murder of a girl who is murdered every singe night. The main character switches bodies every day in an attempt to get different points of view. And yes, it is wild.<br/><br/>So the thing I’ve seen praised about this book is that the plot is <b>ridiculously complex</b>, and it very much is. I am in awe over the tight plotting used in this book. This must have taken a very long outline and the complexity certainly makes this st</span>
  <span id="freeText7723345074377891101" style="display:none"><i>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is a thriller following an investigation into the murder of a girl who is murdered every singe night. The main character switches bodies every day in an attempt to get different points of view. And yes, it is wild.<br /><br />So the thing I’ve seen praised about this book is that the plot is <b>ridiculously complex</b>, and it very much is. I am in awe over the tight plotting used in this book. This must have taken a very long outline and the complexity certainly makes this stand out. I think, however, that the marketing has been very focused on plot twists - I was only <i>seriously</i> shocked by a few twists reading this book, and I’ve already forgotten what, exactly, it was. The delight in this book is not in plot twists, but <b>in seeing the full story come together.</b> I will say that the actual ending, though I predicted parts of it, had enough surprises that it was still delightful. <br /><br />As with many adult thrillers, I struggled to connect to or care about any of the characters. The lead character is almost <i>completely</i> lacking in personality, which makes sense given the entire theme of him being absorbed into bodies, but doesn’t work, as we’re led to believe that he is in constant danger of becoming something awful but never given details to notice or a reason to care. There’s a way of writing a compelling character with amnesia; high motivation, people around them we care about, etc, and this book doesn’t do a great job. I was mostly, however, really disappointed by the <i>bodies</i> Aiden switches into: <b>almost every person he occupies is a dislikable person.</b> Bell is quite boring and later revealed to be terrible, Mr. Collins spends his entire day in agony, Ravencourt is terrible (and for unrelated reasons his section was my absolute least favorite of the book). That’s just the first three, and I will not be going into the rest because they get <i>much</i> worse. <br /><br />Something I really enjoyed about this book, however, was the message - this book is very focused on <b>realizing the changeability of people</b>, and though I never cared about any of these characters much, I did find myself believing in and enjoying the message. I think this message is probably the most daring the book ever gets. <br /><br />..So I actually considered and came very close to rating this book a four star, but I found myself forgetting it very quickly. <b>With a thriller of this type, I usually would have kept my rating a four no matter how much I forgot</b>. <br /><br />However, <b>the fatphobia in this book was <i>utterly ridiculous</i>.</b> I found it rather disturbing to read such an absolute distate from the narrator and author for the fatness of the character he inhabits: Ravencourt is described as a “pig” and a “cow” over and over, and repeatedly described as “disgusting” with seemingly no regard for his humanity. The voyeuristic imagery of fatness is, exclusively and completely, <b>meant to disgust and shock the audience.</b> It is the main thread of a good 20% of the book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141071322" rel="nofollow noopener">a few quotes are stated here</a>, and this reviewer only got to the beginning of this section, at 20%, so can I just say: it’s like, five times that many. I found this incredibly distasteful from about the third comment on, and the near-constant repetition of this rhetoric had me wanting to put the book down. I'm really wondering what the authorial intent is here, and perhaps more importantly, <b>how the author must interact with overweight people in his own life.</b><br /><br />I also felt that rape was used as a plot device in a way that made me somewhat uncomfortable – SPOILER: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a bunch of the book is told through the pov of a person who committed a rape approximately two hours before, and it’s criticized, but… the impacts on the victim are very much ignored. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is a huge and very common issue in literary fiction, but I also hated it and it impacted my enjoyment of this as a thriller.<br /><br />So… despite many good elements, I kind of just want to tell you to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795319518?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Westing Game</a> instead. Nothing but respect for MY president. <br /><br />TW: really intense fatphobia that the author really sounds like he agrees with, suicide, and rape. <br /><br />✨<i>Arc received from the publisher via Netgalley for an honest review.</i> <br /><b>
  <i>release date:</i>
</b> 8 September 2018<br />💜bro read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296946869?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1#comment_form" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_2253270501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2253270501" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2253270501?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408889565" href="/book/show/35967101-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2253270501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11544356625735605257">Stuart Turton has written an extraordinarily original, atmospheric, intelligent and fiendishly complex novel that I really loved! At one level it masquerades as an Agatha Christie style golden age classic crime, and indeed many of the tropes present in that genre are here such as the diverse range of characters at a country house party. It is no exaggeration to say it is so much more, including the presence of time leaps, and absolutely nothing is as it seems. Prior to the murder of Evelyn Hardc</span>
  <span id="freeText11544356625735605257" style="display:none">Stuart Turton has written an extraordinarily original, atmospheric, intelligent and fiendishly complex novel that I really loved! At one level it masquerades as an Agatha Christie style golden age classic crime, and indeed many of the tropes present in that genre are here such as the diverse range of characters at a country house party. It is no exaggeration to say it is so much more, including the presence of time leaps, and absolutely nothing is as it seems. Prior to the murder of Evelyn Hardcastle, there was another death 19 years ago where justice was not fully served. Aiden Bishop is a guest at the party where Evelyn is murdered, he is trapped in a nightmarish Groundhog Day, destined to relive that day until he solves the crime and identifies the murderer. Each day he takes on the body of a different character at the party, with all the consequent complications that ensue, such as the differing friend circles and enemies.<br /><br />Turton gives us a heavily detailed, inventive and ambitious story with beautiful, and lyrical prose. Whilst I found it compulsive reading, it is not a book for everyone, I can see many finding it frustrating. The author is to be congratulated for penning a tale, which whilst occasionally exasperating, allows the reader to exercise their little grey cells! This is a book for those who enjoy being taken out of their comfort zone, enjoy intriguing puzzles and have a penchant for the curious and the strange. A brilliant and twisted read that is never less than enthralling. Many thanks to Bloomsbury for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11544356625735605257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2610573224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2610573224" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2610573224?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/38606428-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2610573224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5031173485904367238">wow. this book is wild! i swear, i spent the majority of the story whispering <i>‘what the heck is going on???’</i> to myself over and over. i still dont even think i know what i just read, i just know i really enjoyed it. <br/><br/>this is a ‘whodunnit’ unlike anything i have read before. mainly because of how ambitious it is. there are so many characters, each with their own role and secrets, which creates multiple plot layers and forces different outcomes for various events, all while a murder is trying to be</span>
  <span id="freeText5031173485904367238" style="display:none">wow. this book is wild! i swear, i spent the majority of the story whispering <i>‘what the heck is going on???’</i> to myself over and over. i still dont even think i know what i just read, i just know i really enjoyed it. <br /><br />this is a ‘whodunnit’ unlike anything i have read before. mainly because of how ambitious it is. there are so many characters, each with their own role and secrets, which creates multiple plot layers and forces different outcomes for various events, all while a murder is trying to be solved! not to mention this story isnt told in chronological order. each ‘host’ wakes up at a different point during the same day, with one man reliving that day eight times. its enough to get anyone confused! but the overwhelming amount of content is what makes this story so exciting! there is just so much to grab onto to that the reader is never left empty-handed. <br /><br />additionally, i love the writing. the story feels like the words of someone who has written their entire life (can we take a moment to appreciate that this is a debut?!?). not because its distinctly flashy or clever. if anything, its a very subtle kind of writing style. but its also the writing style of someone who is confident in their ability, and that kind of tone works so well this particular story and genre. <br /><br />i will admit, because this story asks so much by requiring the reader to steadily keep up with everything that is going on (and trust me, theres a lot), you definitely have to be in the right mood/mindset to read this and willing to make the commitment to see this to the end. so if you are looking for a thrilling murder mystery that will constantly keep you on your toes, then this book is exactly what you need!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5031173485904367238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2555904312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555904312?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492670124" href="/book/show/40914164-the-7-1-2-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=eh">eh</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror-etc">mystery-thriller-horror-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555904312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1045989444460992880">Well, yikes.<br/><br/>Here are the things I knew about this book before starting it:<br/>1) Its original title (and current UK title) was The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle, which, in pure coincidence, is very very similar to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026823954?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Seven Husbands of Evelyn Hugo</a>, and was therefore changed in the US. (I think this is awesome.)<br/>2) It’s a murder mystery with quite possibly the coolest conceit of any book ever. (I think this is awesome.)<br/>3) It’s teeming with gratuitous fat shaming. (I think this is one of the less a</span>
  <span id="freeText1045989444460992880" style="display:none">Well, yikes.<br /><br />Here are the things I knew about this book before starting it:<br />1) Its original title (and current UK title) was The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle, which, in pure coincidence, is very very similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026823954?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Seven Husbands of Evelyn Hugo</a>, and was therefore changed in the US. (I think this is awesome.)<br />2) It’s a murder mystery with quite possibly the coolest conceit of any book ever. (I think this is awesome.)<br />3) It’s teeming with gratuitous fat shaming. (I think this is one of the less awesome things I've ever heard in my life.)<br /><br />Add to that list that the style is extremely overbearing and unyielding over the course of 480 pages (which feels like many more), and you have my list of major takeaways from this reading experience.<br /><br />Let’s go in order.<br /><br />NUMBER 1: TITLE THING<br />Well, we basically already covered this.<br /><br />But it says a lot that I still think this is the most interesting thing about this book, and it has nothing to do with its contents.<br /><br />NUMBER 2: PLOT THING<br />The idea for this book is SO COOL. Which is why it’s extra lame that I found the first 300-ish pages to be very, very boring, and also found the Big Reveal to be - while not predictable - also boring, and generally speaking was very bored by this whole thing.<br /><br />Also, the fact that the conceit of this book is what it is (meaning, a guy wakes up in a different person’s body every day with the task of solving the murder of Evelyn Hardcastle) means there must be Magic involved.<br /><br />Cool! Who doesn’t love magic?<br /><br />Um, apparently this author, because this Magical World goes largely unexplained and then is halfheartedly told at one point but is clearly not the Main Issue.<br /><br />Which is extra, extra lame.<br /><br />NUMBER 3: FATPHOBIA THING<br />Reading this author say that he did not intend to shame fat people in this book is the stupidest, dumbest, most useless excuse for blatant hatred I’ve ever heard.<br /><br />It’s actually worse if the fat shaming in this book is not intended, because the idea that someone could go around subliminally thinking things as hateful as this is absurd. The way the fat character in this is written - traitless but for the fact that he is very fat, and therefore lonely and abhorrent and disgusting - is so awful. It’s to the point of being basically unreadable.<br /><br />This book got better towards the end, but I still wish I had DNFed it at this point.<br /><br />NUMBER 4: STYLE THING<br />I could tell within a couple dozen pages that this style - extremely overwrought, extremely overbearing, and extremely present for the whole book - was not going to work for me.<br /><br />It never did.<br /><br />Bottom line: The only cool thing about this book was the idea behind it, and everything about the execution was a major bummer.<br /><br />-------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />well, i didn't hate this as much as i expected.<br /><br />what a rave review.<br /><br />rtc / 2 stars<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />42 pages into this and already brutally sick of the style. YET ANOTHER PROMISING READING EXPERIENCE</span>

<div id="review_2494698613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2494698613" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2494698613?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=death-is-not-the-end">death-is-not-the-end</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2494698613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2859558280866663035"><b>fulfilling my 2019 goal to read (at least) one book each month that i bought in hardcover and put off reading long enough that it is now in paperback.</b><br/><br/><i>"Funny how things repeat, isn’t it?"</i><br/><br/>i have read a lot of books, but i have never read anything like this. <br/><br/>that’s one of those glib clichés; the book-blurb equivalent of picking a tattoo from the wall, but in this case, it’s the absolute truth. it’s a baller of a debut—an intricately plotted and wholly satisfying mix of sci-fi and mystery; their dif</span>
  <span id="freeText2859558280866663035" style="display:none"><b>fulfilling my 2019 goal to read (at least) one book each month that i bought in hardcover and put off reading long enough that it is now in paperback.</b><br><br><i>"Funny how things repeat, isn’t it?"</i><br><br>i have read a lot of books, but i have never read anything like this. <br><br>that’s one of those glib clichés; the book-blurb equivalent of picking a tattoo from the wall, but in this case, it’s the absolute truth. it’s a baller of a debut—an intricately plotted and wholly satisfying mix of sci-fi and mystery; their different-but-complementary flavors as unexpectedly addictive as m&amp;ms in popcorn. <br><br>any attempt to summarize this book will probably make me sound bonkers, but if you want a touchpoint-parade, it’s basically <i>quantum leap</i> meets <i>groundhog day</i> meets <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15790842.Life_After_Life__Todd_Family___1_" title="Life After Life (Todd Family, #1) by Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Life After Life</a> meets <i>downton abbey</i> meets <i>memento</i> with more twists than… something <i>really</i> twisty. so twisty. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560869852i/27688600._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and this is why no one invites me to pitch meetings. <br><br>i’m glad i *finally* got around to reading this—i enjoyed trying to keep track of all of the layers of paths and people and timelines; attempting to winnow out the book's secrets before their various reveals, squeaking every time that creepy footman made an appearance, and loving the fact that pretty much every body our poor narrator found himself in was a different kind of terrible. <br><br><i>"How splendid it is to be a gentleman."</i><br><br>this is another book that, if a graphic novel version of it were to become available, OH OR A CHOOSE-YOUR-OWN-ADVENTURE (GRAPHIC) NOVEL, i would be very keen on reading it.<br><br>if there’s ever a pitch meeting to make this happen, feel free to invite me to it. i will supply the snacks and similes. and sibilants.<br><br>see you soon, rabbits...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560870089ra/27688628.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2859558280866663035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3592061521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3592061521" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3592061521?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408889510" href="/book/show/43242080-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592061521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14671821529363987874"><i>”How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?”</i><br/><br/>The answer is <b>VERY!</b> Considering that our MC has no memories and wakes up in a totally foreign body this doesn’t really come as a surprise though. I guess we’d all be scared if we’d experience something like that. I mean at first Aiden doesn’t even know his own name, all he knows is a name that dropped from his lips before he witnessed a murder. What a way to start your day! And this is just the first one. <br/><br/>8 days.<br/>8 different hosts. <br/>A hug</span>
  <span id="freeText14671821529363987874" style="display:none"><i>”How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?”</i><br /><br />The answer is <b>VERY!</b> Considering that our MC has no memories and wakes up in a totally foreign body this doesn’t really come as a surprise though. I guess we’d all be scared if we’d experience something like that. I mean at first Aiden doesn’t even know his own name, all he knows is a name that dropped from his lips before he witnessed a murder. What a way to start your day! And this is just the first one. <br /><br />8 days.<br />8 different hosts. <br />A huge manor.<br />A murder. <br />A violent footman.<br />A mysterious Plague Doctor.<br />Several rivals.<br />And innumerable intrigues and lies that entwine around Blackheath like ivy. <br /><br /><i>”The future isn’t a warning my friend, it’s a promise, and it won’t be broken by us.”</i><br /><br />Who can you trust?<br />Who is telling the truth?<br />Who is lying? <br />Who is desperate enough to cut your throat in your sleep? <br /><br /><i>”If this isn’t hell, the devil is surely taking notes.”</i><br /><br />I LOVED this so much! &lt;3 “The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle” was some sort of “Groundhog Day” meets “Every Day” and “Sherlock Holmes”. There were so many different characters in this book and each and every single one of them had their own agenda. To collect all those hints and breadcrumbs, to keep track of the happenings, to know the right order of things, it was quite a challenge! And boy, do I love myself a decent challenge. *lol* In other words: I had so much fun trying to figure out things! There were times my brain cells ended up twisted like a pretzel but this only made everything even more intriguing! XD I already said it in my pre-review and I’ll say it again: I don’t even want to know how many hours Turton invested in all those plot lines! It must have taken ages! Also the mysterious Plague Doctor and the character of the footman added quite some thrill to the story. Aiden isn’t just hunting for the killer but he’s also hunted by the footman and this gave the story such an urgent vibe that I found myself at the edge of my seat! <br /><br /><i>”Everywhere I go, he seems to be a step ahead of me. And yet, simply winning isn’t enough. He needs me to know it. He needs me to be afraid. For some reason, he needs me to suffer.”</i><br /><br />All told, I loved the atmosphere of Blackheath, the countless mysteries that floated around in the air like a seemingly impenetrable wall of mist. Easy lies falling like ripe apples from the lips of corrupted souls, truths that vanished like smoke if you scrutinized them too closely, lies within lies and deceptions that could have filled the entire mansion with their presence. In short: This was brilliant! <br /><br />I won’t say more! This is a book you just need to experience for yourself and it’s definitely worth it! <br /><b>READ IT!!</b> You won’t regret it! ;-)<br /><br />For every one of you who followed my updates closely: I managed to solve at least 2 ½ of the main puzzles and I’m going to share it in the spoiler tag! XD<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />1.) <i>”The Plague Doctor was telling the truth. There’s no escape from Blackheath.”</i><br />I kind of figured that Blackheath is some sort of prison. I mean we got enough hints throughout the entire book, so that one was pretty easy. ;-)<br /><br />2.) <i>”It doesn’t matter whether we like her, or whether the Plague Doctor is right, you don’t get to kill somebody and put them on display. She’s innocent, and we can stop it. And we should.”</i><br /><br />I figured out that Daniel Coleridge was no future host of Aiden. The more I saw of him the more I realized that he couldn’t be. Aiden Bishop was too honourable to be Daniel and the less hosts he had left, the less likely it became that Daniel was one of them. Call it a gut feeling I had pretty early on. <br /><br />3.) I figured out that Michael Hardcastle killed Evelyn. There were a couple of hints we got and I followed them as good as I could. For instance the two black revolvers that looked exactly the same. Aiden asked Michael about them on the hunt and it was that moment when I realized that Evelyn used a white revolver when she killed herself the second time. There was a change in the pattern which only left the conclusion that the black revolver had been changed and from there on it was easy to see the connection to Michael and what it meant that she hadn’t used the black one. <br /><br /> 4.) <i>“This isn’t a celebration, it’s a punishment, and there’ll be fifty people in their very finest clothes watching it happen.”</i><br /><br />Now to Evelyn herself... that got my brain into a real knot. At first I suspected Cunningham to be the murderer of Thomas. He had the opportunity and a motive. After all he was one of the children that went on that scavenger hunt and he was the illegitimate son of Helena Hardcastle and Charlie Carver. Jealousy is a strong motive and he didn’t seem to be happy about his position in the house. But then I got to see more of him and stopped suspecting him. Still, I KNEW, I just knew that one of Helena’s children had to be Thomas’s murderer. She had been covered in blood but it was obvious that she didn’t kill him and so I assumed that she was trying to cover for someone else. One of her own children. A mother would always try to protect her child, no matter what it did. Well, and then I got that little bit that Michael had been at home sick. So who else had an opportunity to kill Thomas and the means to do it? Evelyn. She had a horse, everyone assumed she was out riding and no one could prove where she’d been. And here came my dilemma. I was SO damn certain that Evelyn killed her own brother. I KNEW it! But I just couldn’t align her character with the cunning deed. You see, the Evelyn I got to know throughout the entire book was a good soul. She defended her maid against a rascal; she regretted her decisions, she showed kindness to a man she had despised for his actions. It didn’t fit. How could a person like that be a killer? So I was at a loss. What I never took into consideration was that Felicity was acting as Evelyn Hardcastle and that Evelyn’s maid Madeline Aubert was actually Evelyn. Turton definitely got me there. Even when Millicent Derby and Evelyn’s father were poisoned I didn’t really suspect Evelyn. I didn’t connect Millicent going to the gallery of pictures after seeing Evelyn and her maid next to each other. *lol* And I could bite myself for that mistake. XD In retrospective it all makes sense. I mean who else would want Evelyn to be out of the picture? Michaels poisoning was just an accident because he drank from the same glass Evelyn did. <br /><br />5.) And now to Helena Hardcastle. I knew she wasn’t the killer right from the start. Aiden might have suspected her but she would have never hurt her own children no matter how much she despised them. (She knew Evelyn had killed Thomas, I mean she believed it to be an accident but she never forgave her for it. Yet she still protected her for years.) So since Helena was a no-show the entire book I knew she was dead, which was the reason I suspected Cunningham for a while. He was the last one to see her alive. ;-) You see, if Cunningham would have been Thomas’s murderer he would have a reason to want his mother out of the way, and if Evelyn would have been Thomas’s murderer the same would be valid for her. But Cunningham spoke with his mother and was fond of her and he would have had multiple opportunities to kill her over the years. So what changed? Evelyn appeared on the scene. And once again I was sure Evelyn killed Thomas and Helena but I couldn’t connect it with her character which seemed to be so at odds with those sinister deeds. *LOL* Damn, if I would have made that connection with Madeline. XD <br /><br />6.) And last but not least: I never would have figured out that ALL of the Hardcastle’s children were from Charlie Carver. That one caught me out of the blue. Also Anna’s true identity. Never would have known that if the Plague Doctor wouldn’t have told Aiden. *lol*<br /><br />So I guess that’s all for now! I hope you had fun reading my musings. XD <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />I absolutely loved this!!! &lt;3<br />Like seriously, it was so much fun to collect all those puzzle pieces and breadcrumbs! <br />This book made me think so much and I just loved it for twisting my mind! *lol*<br />Also at least 2 ½ of my main theories were confirmed, which makes me a happy camper! =))<br /><br />Full review to come soon! Stay tuned! ;-)<br /><br />P.S: I don't even want to know how many hours Turton invested in all those plot lines. XD<br />_______________________________<br /><br />This is going to be my first Halloween read of 2020 and I hope it’s going to be a good one! <br />Technically “The Language of Thorns” turned out to be a perfect Halloween book too but this is the first one I actually chose for the spooky time of the year. XD<br /><br />I really like the idea of <b>“The Seven ½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle”</b> and I’m curious to find out if it’s done well. Just imagine waking up in the body of the murderer one day. O_o<br />But then again the murderer doesn’t want Aiden to find out so this is going to be fun. ;-P<br /><br />Also can anyone explain to me why it’s sometimes “The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle” and then it’s “The Seven ½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle”?! I’d really love to know why they changed it.<br />As it seems the title alone is already a mystery. *lol*</span>
  <a data-text-id="14671821529363987874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
