    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2259156670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2259156670" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2259156670?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40033006-the-7-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2259156670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12214552755719866480">I just finished my September 2019 reread for my IRL book club, and I am still in love with this book! Also, I just came up with a completely different theory on what the “7 1/2 deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle” REALLY means, and I’m so curious to know if I’m right. It’s horribly spoilery, and it’s behind spoiler tags at the end of this review. <br/><br/>All the stars! Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-7%C2%BD-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>. <br/><br/>Debut author Stuart Turton’s <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>, originally published earlier this ye</span>
  <span id="freeText12214552755719866480" style="display:none">I just finished my September 2019 reread for my IRL book club, and I am still in love with this book! Also, I just came up with a completely different theory on what the “7 1/2 deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle” REALLY means, and I’m so curious to know if I’m right. It’s horribly spoilery, and it’s behind spoiler tags at the end of this review. <br><br>All the stars! Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-7%C2%BD-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>. <br><br>Debut author Stuart Turton’s <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>, originally published earlier this year in Great Britain as <i>The 7 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>, is an intricately plotted murder mystery, set in an isolated early 20th century English mansion, with a highly imaginative speculative element that is only gradually revealed, as our main character tries to figure out who he really is, and how to solve the mystery of Evelyn Hardcastle’s pending death … or has her death already occurred?<br><br>**I've avoided spoilers BUT I do discuss a part of the basic concept of the book in this review, some of the things that are disclosed around the 12-15% mark, not to mention in the book's blurb. There's definitely something to be said, though, for going into this book completely cold, like I did. If you're interested in doing that, stop reading this review, don't look at anyone else's, and just go read this book! It's worth your time!**<br><br>The plot and setting are worthy of Agatha Christie: Lord and Lady Hardcastle have invited a number of guests to their British country mansion, Blackheath House, for a weekend party to celebrate the return of their daughter, Evelyn, from Paris. (The notable guests and household staff are conveniently listed in a copy of the party invitation at the beginning of the book.) One of the guests, Dr. Sebastian Bell, suddenly comes to himself while running through the forest surrounding Blackheath. The name “Anna” was on his lips, but he has no idea who Anna is or who he himself is. His memory is completely blank. Bell is horrified to see a man chasing a woman through the forest, and then a scream and a pistol shot.<br><br>Eventually Bell, with a little mysterious help, makes his way back to the mansion, where he tries to convince the other guests to search for the woman he is certain was murdered in the forest. But nobody at Blackheath knows (or in any case admits to knowing) a woman named Anna, and they’re dubious about Bell’s improbably story, particularly in light of his amnesia. Bell meets several of the other guests, including Evelyn Hardcastle, a blonde woman in her late twenties who quickly strikes up a friendship with him (“I loathe getting to know people, so whenever I meet somebody I like, I just assume a friendship immediately. It saves a great deal of time in the long run.”) In the late evening Bell sees something that frightens him so much he faints. He wakes up in another person’s body ― the butler, Mr. Collins ― in the morning of the same day that he just lived through as Sebastian Bell. His day as Collins is even more hellish than it was the first time around. And then he wakes up again, early in the morning of that same day, in another person’s body. Is there a way out of this nightmare?<br><br>I went into <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> without knowing anything about its plot; I had conveniently forgotten the blurb by the time I began reading the book. Normally I hate not having context in a novel, and being confused about what the book I’m reading is generally about. But in this case going in blind was highly appropriate, because our main character (who does find out his real name eventually) initially has no idea who he actually is or what is going on around him. The light sheds very gradually, but it all comes together in the end with an awesome set of twists and turns that Dame Christie herself certainly would have admired. Characters often aren’t who they seem, and events that seemed to signify one thing frequently turn out to have an entirely different meaning.<br><br>The plot of <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is so layered, with a tremendously tight timeline and so many interwoven elements and characters, that I can’t help but picture Turton writing this novel in a room filled with vast numbers of Post-it notes and crisscrossing strings tying everything together, like in the old <i>Heroes</i> TV show.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538171638i/26368667.jpg" width="400" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Turton has, in fact, stated that he used a massive spreadsheet, a notepad for each character, and a map of the setting ― as well as the aforementioned Post-it notes ― in the process of writing this book.) The speculative element is fascinating, if slightly far-fetched, but undeniably creative. When the main character realizes that the personalities of his host bodies are leaking through, affecting his thoughts and reactions, it deepens the plot.<br><br>On top of this, Turton adds insightful writing that’s a pleasure to read. I highlighted some sixty passages in the book; some of them were to help me keep track of the plot and characters, but others were simply for the beauty of Turton’s writing.<blockquote>She’s trying to anchor me with words … but I’m impervious to reason, consumed by my hatred for the man I was. His flaws I could accept, perhaps even overcome, but this is a betrayal. He made his mistakes and fled, leaving me holding the tatters of his scorched life.</blockquote>Turton also adds symbolism to <i>The 7½ Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>, including the decaying mansion, Blackheath, which echoes the failings and degeneracies of the upper class characters who are the guests at this dubious house party. A chess piece appears and reappears. A person in the costume of a plague doctor shares information with our main character about his situation and his mission.<br><br>This compelling murder mystery, wrapped in a soft science fiction enigma, is a truly impressive debut novel. Its combination of classic British mystery, <i>Groundhog Day</i> and <i>Quantum Leap</i> blew my mind! I enthusiastically recommend it, and I seriously can’t wait to see what Stuart Turton comes up with next.<br><br>ETA: So here’s my theory about the book’s title. DO NOT open this spoiler unless you’ve read the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Seriously, this ruins the plot! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The real Evelyn killed the following people: Thomas, Michael, Peter, and Helena Hardcastle (her whole family, though Michael’s death was accidental), Millicent Derby, and the stable boy Keith Parker years ago. Plus indirectly Charlie Carver, who was hanged for Thomas’ murder that she committed, and she attempted to murder Felicity Maddox and half-killed her. That’s 7 1/2! Coincidence? I think not. <br><br>P.S. It turns out this actually is one of the questions on Turton's GR author page, and I’m beyond tickled to find out that my theory is right!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12214552755719866480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2346998989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346998989" />
    <a title="Felice Laverne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50404233-felice-laverne"><img alt="Felice Laverne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548611171p2/50404233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346998989?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felice Laverne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felice Laverne" href="/user/show/50404233-felice-laverne">Felice Laverne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408889565" href="/book/show/35967101-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=brit-fic">brit-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=lit-fic">lit-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=full-review">full-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346998989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4076648799526156793"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br/><br/>Whew, what a ride! Stuart Turton’s debut novel is the kind of debut we all yearn for: explosive, energetic, engaging and truly something fresh and new on the scene. <i>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is a brilliant, high-concept murder mystery that had the cogs in my mind turning from the very start (imagine waking up in the forest with no memory of who you are and immediately seeing a young woman murdered!). This, in fact, was the first mystery narrative in a very long time that ha</span>
  <span id="freeText4076648799526156793" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br /><br />Whew, what a ride! Stuart Turton’s debut novel is the kind of debut we all yearn for: explosive, energetic, engaging and truly something fresh and new on the scene. <i>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> is a brilliant, high-concept murder mystery that had the cogs in my mind turning from the very start (imagine waking up in the forest with no memory of who you are and immediately seeing a young woman murdered!). This, in fact, was the first mystery narrative in a very long time that has made me feel like I was part of the story—immersed in the environment—and the first that pulled me in to such a degree that I felt compelled to actively try to unravel the whodunnit mystery right along with the characters. <br /><br /><b>Whodunnit and why!</b> <br /><br />Turton’s atmospheric world is so moody and immersive you’ll feel you should be smoking a pipe with a monocle as you devour it. It was so deliciously wrapped in a sort of British noir, complete with the “party at a country estate” of so many classic murder mysteries. Described by its publisher as “Gosford Park meets Inception by way of Agatha Christie’s Murder on the Orient Express,” this book lived up to the hype and description in a big way! <br /><br />Aiden Bishop is destined to relive the same day over and over again, in eight different bodies, until he can solve the murder of Evelyn Hardcastle. If he does not succeed at the end of that time, the loop restarts and he loses all of his memories of the previous loop, forcing him to start over from scratch with even the basics – who am I? What am I doing here? He realizes that he is both the hunted and the hunter, an innocent and a deceiver, in this highbrow whodunnit. <br /><br /><i>Until now, I’d only witnessed my fellow guests in their handfuls, their spite spread thin across the house. To be ensnared among them all, as I am now, is something else entirely, and the further I descend into the uproar, the thicker their malice seems to become. Most of the men look to have spent the afternoon soaking in their cups and are staggering instead of dancing, snarling and starting, their conduct savage. Young women throw their heads back and laugh, their makeup running and hair coming loose as they’re passed from body to body, goading a small group of wives who’ve grouped together for safety, wary of these panting, wild-eyed creatures. Nothing like a mask to reveal somebody’s true nature…All of this is wrong. The celebration is too desperate. This is the last party before Gomorrah fell…</i><br /><br />The <i>Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> was both intelligent and intellectual, well-paced and deserving of all 500 pages it took up. In a lot of ways, <i>The Seven Deaths</i> was unlike any novel I’ve read before. Skillfully woven together, it was the ultimate literary puzzle. The plot was complex in a baroque but fascinating sort of way, and all the threads Turton spun came together in the end—no stone left unturned, no end left loose. With so many plots converging at once, that was quite the high feat to pull off, but you’ll find it done here superbly in this debut novel. Stuart Turton offers veritable craft in the intricacy of his plotting, a kind of craft that I rarely see anymore. The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle is a mind-bender complete with time leaps and multiple murders seen from multiple angles all on this same day that keeps repeating itself over and over again.<br /><br />The prose was lyrical—honestly, leaning toward flowery—but it is the intricacy of the plot and the atmosphere surrounding these characters that Turton allows to really shine here. Yes, there were moments when this novel graced the line between intricacy and confusion, but it all unraveled splendidly in the end. It was a puzzle of a read; there were moments when the pieces wouldn’t fit and you’d have to scrap it all and start over. For some, that may present as a frustrating experience, but this novel is a real treat to those who love mindbenders, murder mysteries, puzzles and logic games. If that’s you, <b>I highly recommend this novel</b>! Also, if the “Gosford Park/Inception/Agatha Christie" description got your heart racing, then this is the read for you! <i>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i> grabbed me and held me from the very start, probably the most veritable page turner I’ve encountered so far this year, and that’s no easy feat. For such high praise and phenomenal plotting, I give Turton’s debut novel a very strong 4.5 stars. ****<br /><br />*I received an advance-read copy of the book from the publisher, Sourcebooks Landmark, via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /><b>FOLLOW ME HERE:</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49185491-the-other-americans?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=tl37nwckP6&amp;rank=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/queenbee_fifi" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thefelicelaverne/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Other-Americans-Novel-Felice-Laverne/dp/1672094488/ref=sr_1_1?crid=25JA8C7GHLFY8&amp;keywords=the+other+americans+felice+laverne&amp;qid=1579649731&amp;sprefix=the+other+americans+felice%2Caps%2C208&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">Get a Copy of My Book</a> | <a href="https://www.artanddecoagency.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Editing, Author Coaching, Submit Your Book to Me</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4076648799526156793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=united-kingdom">united-kingdom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=netgalley-books">netgalley-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372446573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer626256099369575349"><i> <b>‘’I’m a man in Purgatory, blind to the sins that chased me here.’’</b></i><br/><br/>What would it be like if one day we found ourselves in an another body? What if this happened on a daily basis? Us changing the vessel but retaining most of the traits that make us who we are? What if by changing identities we could turn back the time and prevent an injustice, a horrible crime? This is the wonderful premise of this exquisite novel by Stuart Turton, one of the most unique books of the year.<br/><br/>A man has the opportunit</span>
  <span id="freeText626256099369575349" style="display:none"><i> <b>‘’I’m a man in Purgatory, blind to the sins that chased me here.’’</b></i><br /><br />What would it be like if one day we found ourselves in an another body? What if this happened on a daily basis? Us changing the vessel but retaining most of the traits that make us who we are? What if by changing identities we could turn back the time and prevent an injustice, a horrible crime? This is the wonderful premise of this exquisite novel by Stuart Turton, one of the most unique books of the year.<br /><br />A man has the opportunity to stop the murder of a young woman, Evelyn Hardcastle. In full Groundhog Day mood, he is given eight days and eight identities in which he must find the one responsible for the crime, otherwise everything will become irreversible. So, during a gathering that commemorates a tragic incident in the Hardcastle estate, justice must prevail. However, the wrongs that must be made right reach beyond a single murder…<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’Nothing like a mask to reveal somebody’s true nature.’’</b></i><br /><br />The story is set in Britain, around the late 20s, early 30s from what I could gather and the thing that fascinated me most in this novel isn’t the mystery itself or the unusual background- although they are both brilliant- but the focus on human nature and its various and interminable implications. I can’t even imagine the Herculean task of creating eight different characters to become the vessels of one person, all with their own characteristics and mannerisms and resulting in such a successful and marvelously written story. I admit I was a little bit cautious prior to reading Turton’s book. I thought it would be too confusing or wordy but I couldn’t be more wrong. Obviously, I cannot write a single sentence about the plot but I swear a most solemn vow to you that you will find yourselves with your mouth open in shock for about 60% of the story. That’s how perfect this book is. So many twists, so many different, complicated, tiny pieces of an exciting puzzle. I promise you you won’t be bored or confused. And if you do get confused, it will be in the best way possible.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’Now you see them as I do,’’ says the Plague Doctor, in a low voice. ‘’Actors in a play, doing the same thing night after night’’.</b></i><br /><br />There is seldom such a rich array of characters who are all interesting, secretive, twisted, kind, intelligent, manipulative. Think of any adjective in any language and it will apply perfectly to this perfect cast. As Aidan discovers clues -only to be left in the darkness soon after- so do we. As he meets the guests, as he gets the chance to live inside some of the characters, he gives us the opportunity to collect more evidence. We know nothing before he does and we obtain a much clearer picture of every person involved in the story. How many times can we claim this happens in a mystery? Not even in some of Christie’s finest creations, in my opinion. Personally speaking, the figure of the Plague Doctor was the king of the story. Such a creepy, intimidating, cryptic character that elevated the novel into a whole new level. He embodies the concept of the Mask perfectly since nothing is as it first appears. Everyone undergoes a major transformation and every expectation and belief is turned upside down right until the spectacular ending.<br /><br />I would love to tell you so much more- good, old, blabby me- but I can’t. You absolutely, utterly (...again with the adverbs, I know…) NEED to read <i>The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</i>. It is a reading experience unlike anything we’ve seen and read before. I would like to end this text with a question taken from the Reading Group Guide, included in the book, which I feel captures the psychological weight and the very essence of the entire story.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’If you know someone you loved had a devastating secret, would you choose to find out what it was or love them for who they’ve become? If you knew you did something terrible, would you want to remember or live with that shadow for the rest of your life?’’</b></i><br /><br />Many thanks to Sourcebooks Landmark and NetGalley for the ARC in exchange of an honest review.<br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="626256099369575349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2415483481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2415483481" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408889541" href="/book/show/37632716-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=seasonal-challenges">seasonal-challenges</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2415483481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17294634393922026523">I really don't know how to write a review for this book. Not because I didn't like it, it was fantastic, but because the plot is so intricate and woven I don't want to give anything away. So let's just say it's the story of Aiden, who wakes with no memory at all, just the word 'Anna' on his lips. He finds he's in the middle of a forest, and then manages to stumble across a murder taking place. Aiden is then destined to relive the same day over and over again, until he can solve the murder of Eve</span>
  <span id="freeText17294634393922026523" style="display:none">I really don't know how to write a review for this book. Not because I didn't like it, it was fantastic, but because the plot is so intricate and woven I don't want to give anything away. So let's just say it's the story of Aiden, who wakes with no memory at all, just the word 'Anna' on his lips. He finds he's in the middle of a forest, and then manages to stumble across a murder taking place. Aiden is then destined to relive the same day over and over again, until he can solve the murder of Evelyn Hardcastle.<br /><br />Stuart Turton has done a great job here in his debut novel. As I said the plot is very intricate, but it's never convoluted or confusing, though it may be if you read it over several sittings. My advice is to settle down and read it in a day or two, a big ask I know at over 500 pages, but it would definitely be worth it, just to keep things sharp in your mind. Having said that I found 'The Seven Deaths Of Evelyn Hardcastle' to be one of my best and most rewarding reads this year. Highly recommended.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7992274833181602290"><em>
  <strong>Get ready for the most unusual, overwhelmingly impressive journey through this puzzle land of  "Murder at the Masquerade Ball". </strong>
</em><br/><br/>You won't need a ticket to get in, just get a copy of the book (the hard copy so you can enjoy the map of Blackheath, a cozy and quiet place to read (you won't want any distractions), time to ponder all the twists that are going to keep your brain busy!!<br/><br/>I loved it, but needed to pace myself and take my time to enjoy all the twisty turns that the narrator, Aiden Bish</span>
  <span id="freeText7992274833181602290" style="display:none"><em>
  <strong>Get ready for the most unusual, overwhelmingly impressive journey through this puzzle land of  "Murder at the Masquerade Ball". </strong>
</em><br /><br />You won't need a ticket to get in, just get a copy of the book (the hard copy so you can enjoy the map of Blackheath, a cozy and quiet place to read (you won't want any distractions), time to ponder all the twists that are going to keep your brain busy!!<br /><br />I loved it, but needed to pace myself and take my time to enjoy all the twisty turns that the narrator, Aiden Bishop, threw at me during his attempts to stop a murder that has already taken place!<br /><br />So many times while reading this one, I would have to <em>just pause </em>and smile at the action that was taking place because I was just so amused!!<br /><br />It was so atmospheric and the different players were all very intriguing and kept popping up throughout the story.  Some favorites were the footman, Anna, Evelyn, and the Plague Doctor!<br /><br />I enjoyed my time at Blackheath House and this totally unique reading experience.  I would recommend if you enjoy complex layered mysteries with a large cast of witty characters. It is a book that had me pausing, thinking, and re-reading passages (all the while with a smile :0)<br /><br /><br />I borrowed this book from my library, listened on Hoopla (some chapters), and ended up buying the kindle version half-way through.</span>

<div id="review_2864988783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2864988783" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2864988783?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2864988783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7047227912862054394">This is not 'Gosford Park' meets 'Groundhog Day'. This is 'Friday' meets 'Revolution 9' by way of Miley Cyrus (is she still relevant?). I'm sorry, but this bundle of cheap thrills had no redeeming feature.<br/><br/>The very first paragraph hit me unpleasantly. It was as if a movie had started with the hero walking away from a gigantic explosion that he barely notices. This is like a supercomputer that can beat anyone at chess yet cannot play tic tac toe.<br/><br/>It's not literature in any way shape or form. I hope</span>
  <span id="freeText7047227912862054394" style="display:none">This is not 'Gosford Park' meets 'Groundhog Day'. This is 'Friday' meets 'Revolution 9' by way of Miley Cyrus (is she still relevant?). I'm sorry, but this bundle of cheap thrills had no redeeming feature.<br /><br />The very first paragraph hit me unpleasantly. It was as if a movie had started with the hero walking away from a gigantic explosion that he barely notices. This is like a supercomputer that can beat anyone at chess yet cannot play tic tac toe.<br /><br />It's not literature in any way shape or form. I hope the author never writes another book, as he has struck gold on his first attempt. But however precious gold is, you cannot eat it if you're strung in the wilderness. I felt revolted reading through the pages of this fucking garbage.</span>

<div id="review_2346235345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346235345" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346235345?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36405454-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mystery/thriller fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346235345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11129935756673575664"><b>3.5/5 stars<br/><br/>The less you know about this mystery thriller book, the better your experience will be.</b><br/><br/>First of all, take that rating rounding up or down with a grain of salt, this is a 3.5 stars book for me. As for the review, I honestly have no idea how to review this book, not only mystery/thriller is not my usual read or books that I review, I genuinely think that anything I say can be considered a spoiler for a book like this. I’ll keep this review brief, try to go into this one as blind as poss</span>
  <span id="freeText11129935756673575664" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars<br /><br />The less you know about this mystery thriller book, the better your experience will be.</b><br /><br />First of all, take that rating rounding up or down with a grain of salt, this is a 3.5 stars book for me. As for the review, I honestly have no idea how to review this book, not only mystery/thriller is not my usual read or books that I review, I genuinely think that anything I say can be considered a spoiler for a book like this. I’ll keep this review brief, try to go into this one as blind as possible like I did, it will enrich your experience. I’m going to mention parts that work and didn’t work for me as spoiler-free as possible in the next two paragraphs but feel free to skip reading them if you’re already interested in this book.<br /><br />Let’s start with the parts that work first. This is a debut and it’s a very smart book, consisting of a well-structured storyline with everything coming together in the last 20% of the book. The execution of the conclusion was superbly done and unpredictable. Just when you thought you had everything figured out, Turton keeps you surprised and engaged with revelations. It’s a slow burn but very engaging, I finished this book two days due to how unputdownable it was. I also think the side characters were well developed, especially considering the storytelling method. Prose-wise, this doesn’t feel like a debut at all, Turton’s prose is beautiful, sometimes it felt like reading a literature book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />For the parts that didn’t work, I think the main character’s background should’ve come sooner in the story. It was too late for me to really care about his predicament, I have no idea if this is the usual case with mystery/thriller books though. I mostly enjoyed reading the way the story unfolds but It could've been a better experience if I cared more about the main character. Also, one of the decisions made by the main character near the end of the book need more exposition, it didn’t make sense and didn't sit well with me no matter how I look at it. Lastly, the book went on for a bit too long; there was one part in the middle section, specifically Day 6 chapters, where I was super bored and fell asleep.<br /><br />That’s all. Believe me, this is shorter than my usual reviews and it’s for many good reasons. Bottom line is that <b>if you’re a fan of mystery/thriller book, you really should give this debut a try.</b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/pat/1190-thesevendeathsofevelynhardcastle" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></b> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11129935756673575664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5416592826729172328" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />The early reviews I read of this book were mixed, but the last two months, I’ve watched so many high ratings come in, I succumbed to temptation and requested. This was one of the most challenging reviews I’ve had to write to ensure I didn’t give a speck of the fun away. <br /><br />This book. Wow. The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle is a book you have to give a chance, and if you do, the pay-off is immense if mysteries are your cuppa. <br /><br />I’m offering a basic synopsis because it is best to go into this one with all doors of possibility wide open. <br /><br />Evelyn has been murdered before, countless times. Her parents are throwing a gala, where she will be murdered again. Luckily, Aiden is tasked with solving her murder. <br /><br />Evelyn’s story is detail-laden. Knowing that, it is on my short list of best mysteries because of its originality and refreshing storytelling. <br /><br />As I mentioned above, ample patience is required. It is not a book you will be able to speed through, but if it clicks with you like it did with me, it will be a compulsive, addictive, and impossible to put down. <br /><br />I spent most of the read analyzing and using my noggin trying to piece everything together, and I LOVED THAT. The writing is comforting and warm in its heaviness, and overall, I found The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle to be brilliantly plotted. <br /><br />Thank you to Sourcebooks for the complimentary ARC.     <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42363946-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528378998p2/42363946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2417206161?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/42363946-jenny">Jenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2417206161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17753317925852818231">I’m at a loss for words as where to begin with my review. I don’t know that I will be able to convey into words my love of Stuart Turton’s book, “The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle.” A work of genius and for anyone who loves mysteries or the true old-fashioned “who dunnit”, this is your book. This is not a modern day mystery/thriller but an honest to goodness murder mystery with a multilayered plot. <br/>This work of art requires your complete focus and attention otherwise you might miss one of th</span>
  <span id="freeText17753317925852818231" style="display:none">I’m at a loss for words as where to begin with my review. I don’t know that I will be able to convey into words my love of Stuart Turton’s book, “The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle.” A work of genius and for anyone who loves mysteries or the true old-fashioned “who dunnit”, this is your book. This is not a modern day mystery/thriller but an honest to goodness murder mystery with a multilayered plot. <br />This work of art requires your complete focus and attention otherwise you might miss one of the many crucial details. I found myself going back and rereading pages to make sure I didn’t miss a clue. At times, I felt totally lost but then another clue was revealed and I would be back on track.<br />Turton’s book is not linear in the way the mystery is first revealed and ultimately solved, it will have the feel of taking one step forward and two steps back before the bigger picture becomes clear. He gives us a complex, intelligent and original novel that gave me renewed faith that there are great mystery writers out there with stories that force us to use our brain cells to figure it out. <br />As I was nearing the end of the book, I started to turn the pages a little slower as I wistfully realized this novel was coming to an end. It’s the ultimate paradox, you want to get to the end to see the conclusion but it also means the end of this remarkable experience. <br />As a fan of escape rooms, I love the challenge of trying to solve the mystery to get out of the room. Now imagine solving the mystery, unlocking the room only to find yourself in another room and faced with another mystery and repeating this pattern multiple times before you can escape. Solving the mystery of who killed Evelyn Hardcastle is only the beginning to unraveling the bigger mystery. <br />The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle is a labyrinth, a three dimensional puzzle and a great ride all in one book. Run, don’t walk, to get a copy of this book but then catch your breath, pour yourself a glass of wine and savor each page of one of the best mysteries you will read. <br />I received an advance copy of this book from NetGalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17753317925852818231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2184364853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2184364853" />
    <a title="Ginger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger"><img alt="Ginger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593449448p2/14097149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184364853?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40511119-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184364853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3849288947706590664"><b>4 STARS! ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</b><br/><br/>This is going to be a tough review to write. Not because I didn't love it, but what to say so that I don’t give anything away.<br/>This review is going to be short and to the point. <b>The less you know about this book, the more you will enjoy it!</b><br/><br/><b>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</b> was a mixture of a <i>Agatha Christie</i> novel and the sci-fi television series, <i>Quantum Leap</i>.<br/><br/>So, if you’ve never heard of <i>Quantum Leap</i>, the premise of the television series is the main character Dr. Sam Beckett </span>
  <span id="freeText3849288947706590664" style="display:none"><b>4 STARS! ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</b><br /><br />This is going to be a tough review to write. Not because I didn't love it, but what to say so that I don’t give anything away.<br />This review is going to be short and to the point. <b>The less you know about this book, the more you will enjoy it!</b><br /><br /><b>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</b> was a mixture of a <i>Agatha Christie</i> novel and the sci-fi television series, <i>Quantum Leap</i>.<br /><br />So, if you’ve never heard of <i>Quantum Leap</i>, the premise of the television series is the main character Dr. Sam Beckett (Bakula) is placed in the body of someone else and he has to correct historical mistakes during that episode. I loved it!<br /><br />And <b>The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle</b> has this type of vibe. The main character, Aiden Bishop is placed in a different character each day until something terrible happens to that character. Once that character has died or is no longer in service, he can’t use it again. But while he’s in each character, he must try and figure out who killed Evelyn Hardcastle so that he can escape Blackheath House.<br />There are so many characters in this book that I had to keep looking back at the invite in the front of the book. It has all the characters that are cordially invited to Blackheath House for a masquerade.<br />Trust me, use that to your advantage when this gets a bit complicated.<br /><br />The fact that this was a debut book of <i>Stuart Turton</i> blows my mind. The creativity and writing is just excellent. I wish that the book had been a bit shorter, but he does an excellent job of creating this setting and mystery.<br />And when the murderer is finally revealed, I had no idea!! I'm usually great at solving mysteries since I read this genre all the time but <i>Turton</i> got me this time. Well done sir!!!<br /><br />I really have not read anything like this yet and I loved it!<br /><b>Recommended to mystery lovers and anyone that loves a well-crafted plot of suspense and originality.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3849288947706590664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36405454-the-seven-deaths-of-evelyn-hardcastle">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves thrillers any mystery.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292116230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5742992332311635612">5 deserving stars!!! The best book!! (04/04/19 Update: I cannot believe this will be adapted!)<br/><br/><i>Read for January Buddy Read in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/529911-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddy Reads</a>.</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?<i><br/>This lost, I decide. Precisely this lost.</i></i>
</b><br/><br/>When Bell Sabastian finds himself walking in a forest, lost and stripped of his memories; the only word on his lips a name: Anna, he finds himself utterly terrified. The distant cries of a girl being chased by a murderer and then hearing a bullet go off, doesn</span>
  <span id="freeText5742992332311635612" style="display:none">5 deserving stars!!! The best book!! (04/04/19 Update: I cannot believe this will be adapted!)<br /><br /><i>Read for January Buddy Read in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/529911-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddy Reads</a>.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>How lost do you have to be to let the devil lead you home?<i><br />This lost, I decide. Precisely this lost.</i></i>
</b><br /><br />When Bell Sabastian finds himself walking in a forest, lost and stripped of his memories; the only word on his lips a name: Anna, he finds himself utterly terrified. The distant cries of a girl being chased by a murderer and then hearing a bullet go off, doesn’t help. Scared and shameful to find the girl dead, he waits when the murderer suddenly behind him, gives him a compass and a direction to follow. Without looking back, Bell, with nothing better to do follows in the direction the killer advised him to take, only to find the Blackheath mansion-dark and gray and completely isolated or so it seemed. Read more to know…<br /><br />To be honest, I wrote the above lines when I was still in the beginning of the book, and now it seems so far away. This book makes me wanna read more of the genre, something more confusing, unpredictable and fun! Yes, fun! I must confess that though this is a murder mystery, there were times, I smiled at the cleverness of the story at the most inappropriate times. I was hell bent on finding some clues and maybe I did (some things were easy to find if you look hard), but in the long run, this was a remarkable read. The best thing was that nothing was left unexplained. Every little piece, every clue, every missing part was explained in the end and, and, and…. I fear I’ll spoil it for you. There is so much more to it… I will highly recommend you give this book a chance to confuse you, surprise you and make you fall in love with it. <br /><br />I’ll reread it soon and bug everyone at home to get to it too!<br /><br />I really hope he writes more books! His debut is my new absolute favourite and I’m gonna go find myself a hardcopy. <br /><br />If you have read it already, let me know your thoughts and confusions along the way. Do add spoiler tags for our friends who haven’t. Take a look at my confused states as I went through it:<br />(<i>My last chapter’s thoughts have the thoughts about the end and the outcome.</i>)<br /><br /><b><u>My Thoughts as I Read:</u><br />Chapters 1-4:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So, why didn’t that murderer kill him too? Could it be that Bell too was an accomplice (seems like a reasonable thing), but then why did he have those knife marks? And who was this Anna? The murderer is still out there, I’m kinda sure it’s one of the guests/staff members. Also, about the death of Thomas, could it be related? I am gonna try and not over-analyze anything since that’ll only confuse me further. Plus, he really is a cowardly but good at heart guy. And where is that voice coming from inside his head? Could it not be his? Could it be something he’s undergoing? Like a procedure?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 5 and 6:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What the hell? Who was the stranger? Could it be that all the old guests have been called again? The guests that were present when Thomas was murdered? Maybe to find Charlie Carver’s accomplice? Could Bell be in the helping process? And how the tell did that note from Anna tell him about his burning gloves? Perhaps it wasn’t Anna who died. He didn’t really remember her face.<br /><br />Plus I like Evelyn already! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 7:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, what the hell is happening? A single chess piece? But isn’t this book about the death of Evelyn? And I was right about the same guests being brought back. Could it be that Thomas’s parents are finding the culprit or could it be that since they believe that they can’t do so, they’ll punish them all?<br /><br />Is it weird that I don’t trust Daniel so much? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 8:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why am I smiling? This is so much fun! What if there’s no Anna? Just a name? Anyway, it could be that whosoever called him there didn’t come because of Evelyn’s presence or perhaps calling Sebastian to there was a distraction to place that stupid bloodied rabbit in his room. And that compass, where did that come from? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 9:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Oh, okay. I already know this. I wasn’t sure but this is the book where he wakes up in a different body each day, right? Will he be reliving the same day? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 10:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This reminds me of a movie I watched. A movie where everything was repeated again and again until our hero finished a task. But he came back in the same body again and again and he could change how things happen by the way he reacted. Yes, it was <i>Source Code</i>.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Overall, Chapters 1-10</b><br />So I finished the first 10 chapters and this is so so good! For some reason, I find myself smiling. Probably because of the cleverness of the plot. I hope it remains good till the end.<br /><br /><b>Chapters 11-14:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Some questions: that nurse (or whoever she was) who was sitting next to the butler, who was she? Could she be Anna? I wish Evelyn had revealed something. She knew? That’s unsettling. I must admit, it was clever to leave that note though I wonder what Cunningham would find. Also, whoever was in Daniel seems as irritated as our protagonist. And the footman, that’s like a devil who is after them, making them cautious and faster. I am looking forward to meeting him! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 15:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One thing I don’t understand yet. Alright, everything goes the same way for 8 days. The host’s will and brain is used by the protagonist and other’s like him, but we all know there’s a reason why the hosts are doing the things they are doing-to find about Evelyn. For example, the butler was frozen in place when he saw Sebastian Bell in the rain, but he was frozen because he had been Sebastian the previous day and was only confused and shocked. Why would the real butler freeze in his steps there? Why the real characters did what they did? Little rabbit, is he? Lol. And poor Cunningham but that was a clever way. Also, did the previous people who became Ravencourt try that? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 16-17:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For some weird reason, I think the man chasing them in the morning was also our protagonist. Now, that would be grand, won’t it? Aiden Bishop. If that Plague Doctor knows everything, why did he ask about the name from our protagonist in the beginning? Could it be that he also doesn’t know some stuff? Mrs. Derby sure I clever. Did Evelyn break into the room? Also, where the hell is Cunningham? Could he be involved with someone else? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 18:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don’ think it’s Cunningham or any of the eight hosts. It can’t be. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 19:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[All my amusement is gone too. Her parents are horrible! And they couldn’t even bother to come and announce it themselves! Ughhh! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 20:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, I suspected it might look like a suicide. Yes, why the change of weapons? Could there be something in her drink? I wish one of the hosts is Michael. Will Cunningham still be his friend when he wakes up on another day?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 21-22</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I don’t like his new rascal host. Ew. Maybe he is the one who <i>actually</i> attacks Evelyn and Madeline and then hands over the compass to Bell, but what about the bullet? Could it be the girls? I like Anna, and I hope they all are freed, but I think one would be left behind. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 23:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, I was right! This is somewhat predictable but I am immensely enjoying it. This is fun! So, the Plague Doctor regrets the Aiden voluntarily joined to solve this murder mystery? Well, maybe then they both know each other personally. Or am wrong. I wanna know that since they are solving this mystery, is Evelyn dead in real already and now they are trying to find the murderer or she will be murdered in the future and they are actually trying to avoid it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 24:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Thank God, he is now going to find out about Cunningham. Otherwise that envelope under the chair would’ve caused a huge hole in the plot. So Anna knew him before? Is that it? And why would everyone be afraid of him if he does it right? I wonder what’s plan B. this just got even more interesting! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 25:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What if there’s something in that pond next to which Evelyn kills herself? No? yeah, I doubt it. Stanwin can’t be the murderer. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 26 and 27:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lol, what will happen when Derby wakes up? Could it be one of the rivals who hit him on the head? Or was it Evelyn? Also, yeah, Anna could betray him. I think he remembered Anna’s name because Aiden wanted to start from her. She might be the clue. And all this means that Evelyn Hardcastle died a long time ago. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 28:</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>You’ve been a blight on this world ever since I brought you into it.’</b><br /><br />He brought him into the world? Oh, lol. I get it. Sorry (haha). But on another note, he has the weapon! Yay! P.S. Who broke into Helena’s room and what did he find about Cunningham? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 29:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You know, I’ve not suspected Michael, but for some time, I feel like he’s been mentioned so less. Could he be involved? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 30:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, if today they are finding the killer, why did Evelyn do all that every damn day? Anyway, it could be the Plague Doctor, but I don’t know. Or the other rival or even Anna since she wanted him to be near that rock. Poor Evelyn. And did Millicent just die from just a heart attack? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> You know what I love? That I am still only half-way through the book!<br /><br /><b>Chapter 31:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why did Evelyn look confused when she pulled the trigger? Was she told it would be fake or was it just something natural in her state? Or perhaps she saw someone? Did she herself pull the trigger, or someone shot her before she could? He died, I loved that scene. And the death scene of Evelyn changed. Damn. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 32-34:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, what if Daniel is up to something? Why would he be so trusting? Anyway, I think that the favour he has to ask is ii be there when the footman is to be caught but I cannot be sure since they apparently dropped that chase. Also, it was weird why Gold asked him to stay in the carriage. Will he really give her up if he leaves it? I think he’ll leave the carriage anyway. I really want to see Helena now; it’s been long overdue. Anna has been missing in the last few chapters too and even though she is hiding something, I think she’ll be an ally to Aiden in the end. And Sutcliffe was the same in whose wardrobe Cunningham found the mask?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 35:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Finally met one of the parents and he is such an ass. He sure is hollow and only cares about money. I never really trusted Cunningham and Helena and it’s good to learn they are mother and child. Maybe he is working for her then? Plus who told Cunningham to tell Aiden and give him the message saying <i>all of them</i>? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 36:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was fun. Poor Bell. But very good! Anna won’t show up but I hope it goes well. I think Anna will betray him for some reason. And I hope he doesn’t leave her. I can’t wait to see what happens when this all is done-the mystery unraveled. I wanna know who gets out.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 37:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was twisty. So, did Helena frame her lover? I don’t know if she was involved in killing Thomas, but if she were, was Thomas not her child? Sometimes I wonder if Thomas really is alive. What is Cunningham up to? Just proving that Thomas wasn’t murdered by Carver?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 38-39:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, if Aiden has done this thousands of times, did the footman too? I mean if only one of them is to get out, why didn’t the footman ever win? And why wipe their memories every time the loop is reset? And what clothes did Helena find? Were they Thomas’s? And why was Stanwin surprised at his treatment of Lucy? Are they together or something? Do they have a connection?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 40:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So that was quick! I didn’t expect Daniel to just kill Stanwin like that, and then come out in the open. I wonder how Aiden changes when he is in Daniel’s body. He must be the most powerful host. That red haired girl is Lucy. Damn sure!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 41-43:</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Caution will be my truest friend now.</b><br /><br />Yeah, it better be!<br /><br /><b>‘I don’t know how to get us both out of here, Anna.’<br />‘I know.’<br />‘But I will, I won’t leave without you, I promise.’<br />‘I know that too.’<br />And that’s when she slaps me.<br />‘That’s for murdering me,’ she says, standing on her tiptoes to plant a kiss on the sting. ‘Now, let’s go and make sure the footman doesn’t murder any more of you.’</b><br /><br />This is so sweet! I laughed so much here. A little ease in this otherwise twisted and utterly serious tale. I want to believe Anna too. Maybe she was saving some other host of Aiden, someone who might be more helpful. Maybe she was just saving herself. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 44:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So why did Gold want to be hit on the head by inviting Jim there? Daniel always was shady, but who is he then? Could he be the Plague Doctor?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter45:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Charles? I forgot who was Charles. Cunningham?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 46 and 47:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was a handful. Helena, why the hell are you? Poor Carver :/ And Thomas. And now Daniel!! And why did Thomas bolted? It suggests he was meeting someone at the lake. Probably Helena.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 48-50:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I finally trust Cunningham! So, yeah, someone could be willing to kill the whole family. Could it be Carver now? Okay, what about Michael? Who the hell killed Peter? God, there is just too much information to hold up in my tired and exhausted brain! To be continued tomorrow. It’s just there have been more deaths just than Evelyn’s. Thomas, the stable boy, Millicent, and then there’s Carver who was innocent, and Bell and Gold who have been attacked. And Evelyn’s plan was good but it obviously failed. Someone did shoot her though.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 51:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was so good. I wish Jim didn’t die. He was so much help. Michael was going to kill her. I had my doubts about him but I didn’t think he’d do it of kindness. So, when does Evelyn die? And I did suspect Millicent’s death being a murder.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 52:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Our Aiden is quick to forget, isn’t he? He got out of the carriage, he is now going with Daniel to somehow spill his own secrets…<br /><br />So, I read it, and damn! But I still hope Gold won’t be so crazy today. It’s the last damn day. I wonder why the Plague Doctor cares about Aiden so much. Is Anna going to betray him again? Where the hell was she? I do pity Daniel.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 53:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This was so intense. He came for revenge and he took it. He took it until he forgot his sister, his vengeance, his own self. And Oliver, I wonder how he is still sane. I couldn’t see Anna for the leader of those groups. It’s a huge thing he does for Anna, to meet her even when he knows she killed his sister. Looks like Blackheath has rehabilitated him too. Now, let’s get on with Millicent. I also want Daniel out! Is it too much to ask?? I wonder what he did to get in here! Wouldn’t it be grand if he were Anna’s accomplice in real life? This story seemed to have stemmed out from Science-Fiction and I’m not wrong.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 54:<b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What is he going to paint? This is so so so soooo good!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 55:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh wow. She does seem to have changed. I wonder why she had Dance and the butler killed, and even Derby by having him stand next to the rock. Was it because she was forced?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapters 56 and 57:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Another amazing chapter! Thank God, he’s dead. But he was a remarkable character. Will the butler wake up again? You know, I kept waiting for Anna to shoot the butler too, lol. Guess she is trustworthy, eh?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 58:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Did the stable boy’s father do it? But he was too scared when Dance asked him. He couldn’t be it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 59:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Shit! Damn! Wow! Felicity to the rescue. Will the Plague doctor free Anna because she risked her life for Aiden? Or will he still ask for an answer? And Michael lied… he was going to kill Felicity for his psycho sister. He was an act all that time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Chapter 60:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This felt good. I hated Evelyn. She just left the poor boy there and killed her brother. Two brothers remained but Cunningham didn't matter to her, she did loved Michael a lot who was ready to kill for her. Look like she <i>did look ill</i> in his years or perhaps his love for her blinded him. Oliver might be punished but he was a good man, someone with a conscience. Anna and Aiden, both, became better people, though Daniel sure didn’t. He did have a clever host though. I thought they’d simply wake up and find themselves, but maybe they’ll sleep first? Doesn’t matter (does matter), I loved it! Every moment of it. Maybe it was wise to let go of the past, maybe Anna should too. But it’s hard in its own way.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Check out this amazing review from a friend:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2300903860?comment=187924117#comment_187924117" rel="nofollow noopener">PattyMacDotComma's Review</a></b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5742992332311635612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SHO843mZVvIIA2R2FERVRFiNIQAjGGYPT7GTpoQ8Fqghaqks2FRWe/dHDAR1QfSGblEiq7N9aUHy8hm9PjTstg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y1mxT/GxGazS4lCZbMWkSxjc50/8l0nPP2sRYK21ZMSiQKSAUHwZJS2mOOsNwAWJLgDk5GzyRoGCKJt7F72e2g==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/17160667.Stuart_Turton">About Stuart Turton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/17160667.Stuart_Turton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1537181882p3/17160667.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/17160667.Stuart_Turton">Stuart Turton

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1430620033980421677">Stuart lives in London with his amazing wife and daughter. He drinks lots of tea.<br/><br/>What else?<br/><br/>​When he left university he went travelling for three months and stayed away for five years. Every time his parents asked when he’d be back he told them next week, and meant it.<br/><br/>Stuart is not to be trusted. In the nicest possible way. <br/><br/>He’s got a degree in English and Philosophy, which makes him excellent at a</span>
  <span id="freeText1430620033980421677" style="display:none">Stuart lives in London with his amazing wife and daughter. He drinks lots of tea.<br /><br />What else?<br /><br />​When he left university he went travelling for three months and stayed away for five years. Every time his parents asked when he’d be back he told them next week, and meant it.<br /><br />Stuart is not to be trusted. In the nicest possible way. <br /><br />He’s got a degree in English and Philosophy, which makes him excellent at arguing and terrible at choosing degrees. <br /><br />Having trained for no particular career, he has dabbled in most of them. He stocked shelves in a Darwin bookshop, taught English in Shanghai, worked for a technology magazine in London, wrote travel articles in Dubai, and now he’s a freelance journalist. None of this was planned, he just kept getting lost on his way to other places.<br /><br />He likes a chat. He likes books. He likes people who write books and people who read books. He doesn’t know how to write a biography, so should probably stop before he tells you about his dreams or something. It was lovely to meet you, though.<br /><br />Stuart's debut novel is called The Seven Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle in the UK and The 7 1/2 Deaths of Evelyn Hardcastle in the US. They're the same book. Don't fret.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1430620033980421677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
